</div>
			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Palm oil</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
								<div id="contentSub"></div>
												<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
				</div>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Huile_de_palme_biologique_350g.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Huile_de_palme_biologique_350g.jpg/220px-Huile_de_palme_biologique_350g.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Huile_de_palme_biologique_350g.jpg/330px-Huile_de_palme_biologique_350g.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Huile_de_palme_biologique_350g.jpg/440px-Huile_de_palme_biologique_350g.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Huile_de_palme_biologique_350g.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Palm oil block showing the lighter color that results from boiling</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>Palm oil</b> (also known as <b>dendê oil</b>, from Portuguese) is an edible <a href="/wiki/Vegetable_oil" title="Vegetable oil">vegetable oil</a> derived from the <a href="/wiki/Fruit_anatomy#Mesocarp" title="Fruit anatomy">mesocarp</a> (reddish pulp) of the fruit of the <a href="/wiki/Elaeis" title="Elaeis">oil palms</a>, primarily the African oil palm <i><a href="/wiki/Elaeis_guineensis" title="Elaeis guineensis">Elaeis guineensis</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> and to a lesser extent from the American oil palm <i><a href="/wiki/Elaeis_oleifera" title="Elaeis oleifera">Elaeis oleifera</a></i> and the maripa palm <i><a href="/wiki/Attalea_maripa" title="Attalea maripa">Attalea maripa</a></i>.</p>
<p>Palm oil is naturally reddish in color because of a high <a href="/wiki/Beta-carotene" class="mw-redirect" title="Beta-carotene">beta-carotene</a> content. It is not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Palm_kernel_oil" title="Palm kernel oil">palm kernel oil</a> derived from the <a href="/wiki/Palm_kernel" title="Palm kernel">kernel</a> of the same fruit,<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> or <a href="/wiki/Coconut_oil" title="Coconut oil">coconut oil</a> derived from the kernel of the coconut palm (<i><a href="/wiki/Cocos_nucifera" class="mw-redirect" title="Cocos nucifera">Cocos nucifera</a></i>). The differences are in color (raw palm kernel oil lacks <a href="/wiki/Carotenoids" class="mw-redirect" title="Carotenoids">carotenoids</a> and is not red), and in <a href="/wiki/Saturated_fat" title="Saturated fat">saturated fat</a> content: palm mesocarp oil is 49% saturated, while palm kernel oil and coconut oil are 81% and 86% saturated fats, respectively.</p>
<p>Along with coconut oil, palm oil is one of the few highly saturated <a href="/wiki/Vegetable_fat" class="mw-redirect" title="Vegetable fat">vegetable fats</a> and is semisolid at room temperature.<sup id="cite_ref-Plant_cholesterol_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Plant_cholesterol-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>Palm oil is a common cooking ingredient in the tropical belt of <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a> and parts of <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>. Its use in the commercial food industry in other parts of the world is widespread because of its lower cost<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> and the high oxidative stability (<a href="/wiki/Saturated_fat" title="Saturated fat">saturation</a>) of the refined product when used for frying.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>The use of palm oil in food products has attracted the concern of environmental activist groups; the high oil yield of the trees has encouraged wider cultivation, leading to the clearing of forests in parts of Indonesia and Malaysia to make space for oil-palm <a href="/wiki/Monoculture" title="Monoculture">monoculture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> This has resulted in significant acreage losses of the natural habitat of the <a href="/wiki/Orangutan" title="Orangutan">orangutan</a>, of which both species are endangered; one species in particular, the <a href="/wiki/Sumatran_orangutan" title="Sumatran orangutan">Sumatran orangutan</a>, has been listed as <a href="/wiki/Critically_endangered" title="Critically endangered">critically endangered</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> In 2004, an industry group called the <a href="/wiki/Roundtable_on_Sustainable_Palm_Oil" title="Roundtable on Sustainable Palm Oil">Roundtable on Sustainable Palm Oil</a> was formed to work with the palm oil industry to address these concerns.<sup id="cite_ref-Gilbert_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gilbert-9">[9]</a></sup> Additionally, in 1992, in response to concerns about deforestation, the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Malaysia" title="Government of Malaysia">Government of Malaysia</a> pledged to limit the expansion of palm oil plantations by retaining a minimum of half the nation's land as forest cover.<sup id="cite_ref-Morales_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Morales-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Scott-Thomas2_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scott-Thomas2-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_oil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Elaeis_guineensis_MS_3467.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Elaeis_guineensis_MS_3467.jpg/300px-Elaeis_guineensis_MS_3467.jpg" width="300" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Elaeis_guineensis_MS_3467.jpg/450px-Elaeis_guineensis_MS_3467.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Elaeis_guineensis_MS_3467.jpg/600px-Elaeis_guineensis_MS_3467.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2304" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Elaeis_guineensis_MS_3467.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Oil_palm" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil palm">Oil palms</a> (<i>Elaeis guineensis</i>)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Human use of oil palms may date as far back as 5,000 years; in the late 1800s, archaeologists discovered a substance that they concluded was originally palm oil in a tomb at <a href="/wiki/Abydos,_Egypt" title="Abydos, Egypt">Abydos</a> dating back to 3,000 BCE.<sup id="cite_ref-Kiple_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kiple-12">[12]</a></sup> It is believed that Arab traders brought the oil palm to Egypt.<sup id="cite_ref-Obahiagbon_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Obahiagbon-13">[13]</a></sup> Some argue that it is not possible that Arab traders could have brought the oil palm to ancient Egypt, as the Arabs did not settle in Africa until the 8th century CE. It is more likely that the oil palm was brought to Ancient Egypt (Kemet) by its founding peoples who migrated from other regions of the African continent.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>Palm oil from <i>E. guineensiss</i> has long been recognized in <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_Africa" title="Central Africa">Central African</a> countries, and is widely used as a <a href="/wiki/Cooking_oil" title="Cooking oil">cooking oil</a>. European merchants trading with West Africa occasionally purchased palm oil for use as a cooking oil in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>.</p>
<p>Palm oil became a highly sought-after commodity by <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">British</a> traders, for use as an industrial <a href="/wiki/Lubricant" title="Lubricant">lubricant</a> for machinery during Britain's <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>Palm oil formed the basis of <a href="/wiki/Soap" title="Soap">soap</a> products, such as <a href="/wiki/Lever_Brothers" title="Lever Brothers">Lever Brothers</a>' (now <a href="/wiki/Unilever" title="Unilever">Unilever</a>) "<a href="/wiki/Sunlight_(cleaning_product)" title="Sunlight (cleaning product)">Sunlight</a>" soap, and the American <a href="/wiki/Palmolive_(soap)" class="mw-redirect" title="Palmolive (soap)">Palmolive</a> brand.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>By around 1870, palm oil constituted the primary export of some West African countries, such as <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>, although this was overtaken by <a href="/wiki/Cocoa_bean" title="Cocoa bean">cocoa</a> in the 1880s.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2007)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Composition">Composition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_oil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Composition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fatty_acids">Fatty acids</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_oil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Fatty acids">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Fatty_acid" title="Fatty acid">Fatty acid</a></div>
<p>Palm oil, like all <a href="/wiki/Fat" title="Fat">fats</a>, is composed of <a href="/wiki/Fatty_acid" title="Fatty acid">fatty acids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ester" title="Ester">esterified</a> with <a href="/wiki/Glycerol" title="Glycerol">glycerol</a>. Palm oil has an especially high concentration of saturated fat, specifically, of the 16-carbon saturated fatty acid <a href="/wiki/Palmitic_acid" title="Palmitic acid">palmitic acid</a>, to which it gives its name. Monounsaturated <a href="/wiki/Oleic_acid" title="Oleic acid">oleic acid</a> is also a major constituent of palm oil. Unrefined palm oil is a significant source of <a href="/wiki/Tocotrienol" title="Tocotrienol">tocotrienol</a>, part of the <a href="/wiki/Vitamin_E" title="Vitamin E">vitamin E</a> family.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-oil_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oil-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>The approximate concentration of fatty acids in palm oil is:<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<div class="barbox" style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:400px; background: white;">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Carotenes">Carotenes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_oil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Carotenes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Red palm oil is rich in carotenes, such as <a href="/wiki/Alpha-carotene" class="mw-redirect" title="Alpha-carotene">alpha-carotene</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beta-carotene" class="mw-redirect" title="Beta-carotene">beta-carotene</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lycopene" title="Lycopene">lycopene</a>, which give it a characteristic dark red color.<sup id="cite_ref-oil_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oil-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Processing_and_use">Processing and use</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_oil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Processing and use">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Many <a href="/wiki/Processed_food" class="mw-redirect" title="Processed food">processed foods</a> either contain palm oil or various ingredients derived from it.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_Panorama_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Panorama-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Refining">Refining</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_oil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Refining">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Cooking_oil#Refinement" title="Cooking oil">Cooking oil refinement</a></div>
<p>After <a href="/wiki/Mill_(grinding)" title="Mill (grinding)">milling</a>, various palm oil products are made using <a href="/wiki/Refinery" title="Refinery">refining</a> processes. First is <a href="/wiki/Fractionation" title="Fractionation">fractionation</a>, with crystallization and separation processes to obtain solid (<a href="/wiki/Stearin" title="Stearin">stearin</a>), and liquid (<a href="/wiki/Olein" class="mw-redirect" title="Olein">olein</a>) fractions.<sup id="cite_ref-Asianagro_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Asianagro-22">[22]</a></sup> Then melting and <a href="/wiki/Degumming" class="mw-redirect" title="Degumming">degumming</a> removes impurities. Then the oil is filtered and bleached. Physical refining<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (September 2012)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> removes smells and coloration to produce "refined, bleached and deodorized palm oil" (RBDPO) and free sheer fatty acids,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (September 2012)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> which are used in the manufacture of <a href="/wiki/Soap" title="Soap">soaps</a>, <a href="/wiki/Washing_powder" class="mw-redirect" title="Washing powder">washing powder</a> and other products. RBDPO is the basic palm oil product sold on the world's commodity markets. Many companies fractionate it further to produce <a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_olein&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Palm olein (page does not exist)">palm olein</a> for cooking oil, or process it into other products.<sup id="cite_ref-Asianagro_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Asianagro-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Red_palm_oil">Red palm oil</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_oil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Red palm oil">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since the mid-1990s, red palm oil has been <a href="/wiki/Vegetable_fats_and_oils#Extraction" class="mw-redirect" title="Vegetable fats and oils">cold-pressed</a> and bottled for use as cooking oil, and blended into <a href="/wiki/Mayonnaise" title="Mayonnaise">mayonnaise</a> and <a href="/wiki/Salad_oil" class="mw-redirect" title="Salad oil">salad oil</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Butter_and_trans_fat_substitute">Butter and trans fat substitute</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_oil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Butter and trans fat substitute">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The highly saturated nature of palm oil renders it solid at room temperature in temperate regions, making it a cheap <a href="/wiki/Fat_substitute" title="Fat substitute">substitute</a> for <a href="/wiki/Butter" title="Butter">butter</a> or <a href="/wiki/Trans_fat" title="Trans fat">trans fats</a> in uses where solid fat is desirable, such as the making of <a href="/wiki/Pastry" title="Pastry">pastry</a> dough and baked goods. A recent rise in the use of palm oil in the food industry has partly come from changed labelling requirements that have caused a switch away from using trans fats.<sup id="cite_ref-Koh_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Koh-24">[24]</a></sup> Palm oil has been found to be a reasonable replacement for trans fats;<sup id="cite_ref-Heller_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heller-25">[25]</a></sup> however, a small study conducted in 2009 found that palm oil may not be a good substitute for trans fats for individuals with already-elevated LDL levels.<sup id="cite_ref-ScienceDaily_LLC_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ScienceDaily_LLC-26">[26]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/USDA" class="mw-redirect" title="USDA">USDA</a> agricultural research service states that palm oil is not a healthy substitute for <a href="/wiki/Trans_fats" class="mw-redirect" title="Trans fats">trans fats</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biomass_and_bioenergy">Biomass and bioenergy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_oil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Biomass and bioenergy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Palm oil is used to produce both methyl ester and hydrodeoxygenated <a href="/wiki/Biodiesel" title="Biodiesel">biodiesel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Rojas_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rojas-28">[28]</a></sup> Palm oil methyl ester is created through a process called <a href="/wiki/Transesterification" title="Transesterification">transesterification</a>. Palm oil biodiesel is often blended with other fuels to create palm oil biodiesel blends.<sup id="cite_ref-JMSE_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JMSE-29">[29]</a></sup> Palm oil biodiesel meets the European <a href="/wiki/EN_14214" title="EN 14214">EN 14214</a> standard for biodiesels.<sup id="cite_ref-Rojas_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rojas-28">[28]</a></sup> Hydrodeoxygenated biodiesel is produced by direct <a href="/wiki/Hydrogenolysis" title="Hydrogenolysis">hydrogenolysis</a> of the fat into alkanes and propane. The world's largest palm oil biodiesel plant is the Finnish-operated <a href="/wiki/Neste_(company)" class="mw-redirect" title="Neste (company)">Neste Oil</a> biodiesel plant in <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, which opened in 2011 and produces hydrodeoxygenated <a href="/wiki/NEXBTL" title="NEXBTL">NEXBTL</a> biodiesel.<sup id="cite_ref-Yahya_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahya-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>The organic waste matter that is produced when processing oil palm, including oil palm shells and oil palm fruit bunches, can also be used to produce energy. This waste material can be converted into pellets that can be used as a biofuel.<sup id="cite_ref-Choong_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Choong-31">[31]</a></sup> Additionally, palm oil that has been used to fry foods can be converted into methyl esters for biodiesel. The used cooking oil is chemically treated to create a biodiesel similar to petroleum diesel.<sup id="cite_ref-JOPR_2006_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JOPR_2006-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_wound_care">In wound care</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_oil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: In wound care">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Although palm oil is applied to wounds for its supposed <a href="/wiki/Antimicrobial" title="Antimicrobial">antimicrobial</a> effects, research does not confirm its effectiveness.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Production">Production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_oil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 2012, the annual revenue received by Indonesia and Malaysia together, the top two producers of palm oil, was $40 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-sciam201212_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sciam201212-34">[34]</a></sup> Between 1962 and 1982 global exports of palm oil increased from around half a million to 2.4 million tonnes annually and in 2008 world production of palm oil and palm kernel oil amounted to 48 million tonnes. According to FAO forecasts by 2020 the global demand for palm oil will double, and triple by 2050.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:552px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2013palm_oil.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/2013palm_oil.png/550px-2013palm_oil.png" width="550" height="241" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/2013palm_oil.png/825px-2013palm_oil.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/2013palm_oil.png/1100px-2013palm_oil.png 2x" data-file-width="1425" data-file-height="625" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2013palm_oil.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A map of world palm oil output, 2013.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Indonesia">Indonesia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_oil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Indonesia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Palm_oil_production_in_Indonesia" title="Palm oil production in Indonesia">Palm oil production in Indonesia</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> is the world's largest producer of palm oil, surpassing Malaysia in 2006, producing more than 20.9 million tonnes.<sup id="cite_ref-sciam201212_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sciam201212-34">[34]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Indonesia expects to double production by the end of 2030.<sup id="cite_ref-Gilbert_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gilbert-9">[9]</a></sup> At the end of 2010, 60 percent of the output was exported in the form of crude palm oil.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/FAO" class="mw-redirect" title="FAO">FAO</a> data show production increased by over 400% between 1994 and 2004, to over 8.66 million metric tonnes.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Malaysia">Malaysia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_oil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Malaysia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Palm_oil_production_in_Malaysia" title="Palm oil production in Malaysia">Palm oil production in Malaysia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Oilpalm_malaysia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Oilpalm_malaysia.jpg/250px-Oilpalm_malaysia.jpg" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Oilpalm_malaysia.jpg/375px-Oilpalm_malaysia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Oilpalm_malaysia.jpg/500px-Oilpalm_malaysia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Oilpalm_malaysia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A palm oil plantation in Malaysia.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2012, <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, the world's second largest producer of palm oil,<sup id="cite_ref-Pakiam_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pakiam-38">[38]</a></sup> produced 18.79 million tonnes of crude palm oil on roughly 5,000,000 hectares (19,000&#160;sq&#160;mi) of land.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Star_January_2013_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Star_January_2013-39">[39]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USDA2012_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USDA2012-40">[40]</a></sup> Though Indonesia produces more palm oil, Malaysia is the world's largest exporter of palm oil having exported 18 million tonnes of palm oil products in 2011. <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> are the primary importers of Malaysian palm oil products.<sup id="cite_ref-AOCS_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AOCS-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Oil_palm_plantation_in_Cigudeg-03.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Oil_palm_plantation_in_Cigudeg-03.jpg/250px-Oil_palm_plantation_in_Cigudeg-03.jpg" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Oil_palm_plantation_in_Cigudeg-03.jpg/375px-Oil_palm_plantation_in_Cigudeg-03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Oil_palm_plantation_in_Cigudeg-03.jpg/500px-Oil_palm_plantation_in_Cigudeg-03.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Oil_palm_plantation_in_Cigudeg-03.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A palm oil plantation in Indonesia.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nigeria">Nigeria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_oil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Nigeria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As of 2011, <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> was the third-largest producer, with approximately 2.3&#160;million hectares (5.7<span style="margin-left:0.2em">×<span style="margin-left:0.1em">10</span></span><s style="display:none">^</s><sup>6</sup> acres) under cultivation. Until 1934, Nigeria had been the world's largest producer. Both small- and large-scale producers participated in the industry.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Thailand">Thailand</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_oil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Thailand">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2013, Thailand produced 2.0 million tonnes of crude palm oil on roughly 626 thousand hectares. Thailand expects to produce 11 million tonnes of fresh palm nuts in 2016, down from more than 12 million in 2015, the shortfall due to Thailand's drought.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colombia">Colombia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_oil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Colombia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the 1960s, about 18,000 hectares (69&#160;sq&#160;mi) were planted with palm. <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a> has now become the largest palm oil producer in the Americas, and 35% of its product is exported as biofuel. In 2006, the Colombian plantation owners' association, Fedepalma, reported that oil palm cultivation was expanding to 1,000,000 hectares (3,900&#160;sq&#160;mi). This expansion is being funded, in part, by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Agency_for_International_Development" title="United States Agency for International Development">United States Agency for International Development</a> to resettle disarmed <a href="/wiki/Paramilitary" title="Paramilitary">paramilitary</a> members on arable land, and by the Colombian government, which proposes to expand land use for exportable cash crops to 7,000,000 hectares (27,000&#160;sq&#160;mi) by 2020, including oil palms. Fedepalma states that its members are following sustainable guidelines.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some Afro-Colombians claim that some of these new plantations have been expropriated from them after they had been driven away through poverty and civil war, while armed guards intimidate the remaining people to further depopulate the land, with <a href="/wiki/Coca" title="Coca">coca</a> production and trafficking following in their wake.<sup id="cite_ref-dollar_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dollar-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_countries">Other countries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_oil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Other countries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Malayasia_iko_2002169.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Malayasia_iko_2002169.jpg/350px-Malayasia_iko_2002169.jpg" width="350" height="233" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Malayasia_iko_2002169.jpg/525px-Malayasia_iko_2002169.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Malayasia_iko_2002169.jpg/700px-Malayasia_iko_2002169.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="480" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Malayasia_iko_2002169.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A satellite image showing deforestation in <a href="/wiki/Malaysian_Borneo" class="mw-redirect" title="Malaysian Borneo">Malaysian Borneo</a> to allow the plantation of <a href="/wiki/Oil_palm" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil palm">oil palm</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Benin">Benin</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_oil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Benin">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Palm is native to the wetlands of western Africa, and south <a href="/wiki/Benin" title="Benin">Benin</a> already hosts many palm plantations. Its 'Agricultural Revival Programme' has identified many thousands of hectares of land as suitable for new oil palm export plantations. In spite of the economic benefits, <a href="/wiki/Non-governmental_organisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-governmental organisation">Non-governmental organisations</a> (NGOs), such as <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nature_Tropicale&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Nature Tropicale (page does not exist)">Nature Tropicale</a>, claim biofuels will compete with domestic food production in some existing prime agricultural sites. Other areas comprise <a href="/wiki/Peat" title="Peat">peat land</a>, whose drainage would have a deleterious environmental impact. They are also concerned <a href="/wiki/Genetic_modification" class="mw-redirect" title="Genetic modification">genetically modified</a> plants will be introduced into the region, jeopardizing the current premium paid for their non-GM crops.<sup id="cite_ref-wrm_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wrm-47">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cameroon">Cameroon</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_oil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Cameroon">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a> had a production project underway initiated by Herakles Farms in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> However, the project was halted under the pressure of civil society organizations in Cameroon. Before the project was halted, Herakles left the Roundtable on Sustainable Palm Oil early in negotiations.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> The project has been controversial due to opposition from villagers and the location of the project in a sensitive region for biodiversity.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Kenya">Kenya</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_oil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Kenya">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a>'s domestic production of edible oils covers about a third of its annual demand, estimated at around 380,000 metric tonnes. The rest is imported at a cost of around US$140 million a year, making edible oil the country's second most important import after petroleum. Since 1993 a new <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_(biology)" title="Hybrid (biology)">hybrid</a> variety of cold-tolerant, high-yielding oil palm has been promoted by the <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Agriculture_Organization_of_the_United_Nations" class="mw-redirect" title="Food and Agriculture Organization of the United Nations">Food and Agriculture Organization of the United Nations</a> in western Kenya. As well as alleviating the country's deficit of edible oils while providing an important cash crop, it is claimed to have environmental benefits in the region, because it does not compete against food crops or native vegetation and it provides stabilisation for the soil.<sup id="cite_ref-fao_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fao-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ghana">Ghana</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_oil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Ghana">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a> has a lot of <a href="/wiki/Arecaceae" title="Arecaceae">palm nut</a> species, which may become an important contributor to the agriculture of the region. Although Ghana has multiple palm species, ranging from local palm nuts to other species locally called agric, it was only marketed locally and to neighboring countries. Production is now expanding as major investment funds are purchasing plantations, because Ghana is considered a major growth area for palm oil.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Markets">Markets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_oil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Markets">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Palm_oil&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(January 2015)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>According to the Hamburg-based <i>Oil World</i> trade journal,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> in 2008 global production of oils and fats stood at 160 million tonnes. Palm oil and palm kernel oil were jointly the largest contributor, accounting for 48 million tonnes, or 30% of the total output. <a href="/wiki/Soybean_oil" title="Soybean oil">Soybean oil</a> came in second with 37 million tonnes (23%). About 38% of the oils and fats produced in the world were shipped across oceans. Of the 60.3 million tonnes of oils and fats exported around the world, palm oil and palm kernel oil made up close to 60%; <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, with 45% of the market share, dominated the palm oil trade.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food_label_regulations">Food label regulations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_oil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Food label regulations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Previously, palm oil could be listed as "vegetable fat" or "vegetable oil" on food labels in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (EU). From December 2014, food packaging in the EU is no longer allowed to use the generic terms "vegetable fat" or "vegetable oil" in the ingredients list. Food producers are required to list the specific type of vegetable fat used, including palm oil. Vegetable oils and fats can be grouped together in the ingredients list under the term "vegetable oils" or "vegetable fats" but this must be followed by the type of vegetable origin (e.g. palm, sunflower or rapeseed) and the phrase "in varying proportions".<sup id="cite_ref-GAIN_Report_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GAIN_Report-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Supply_chain_institutions">Supply chain institutions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_oil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Supply chain institutions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <b>Roundtable on Sustainable Palm Oil</b> (RSPO) was established in 2004<sup id="cite_ref-Browne_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browne-53">[53]</a></sup> following concerns raised by non-governmental organizations about environmental impacts resulting from palm oil production. The organization has established international standards for sustainable palm oil production.<sup id="cite_ref-Gunasegaran_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gunasegaran-54">[54]</a></sup> Products containing <b>Certified Sustainable Palm Oil (CSPO)</b> can carry the RSPO trademark.<sup id="cite_ref-Yulisman_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yulisman-55">[55]</a></sup> Members of the RSPO include palm oil producers, environmental groups, and manufacturers who use palm oil in their products.<sup id="cite_ref-Browne_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browne-53">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gunasegaran_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gunasegaran-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>The RSPO is applying different types of programmes to supply palm oil to producers.<sup id="cite_ref-GreenPalm_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GreenPalm-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Book and claim: no guarantee that the end product contains certified sustainable palm oil, supports RSPO-certified growers and farmers</li>
<li>Identity preserved: the end user is able to trace the palm oil back to a specific single mill and its supply base (plantations)</li>
<li>Segregated: this option guarantees that the end product contains certified palm oil</li>
<li>Mass balance: the refinery is only allowed to sell the same amount of mass balance palm oil as the amount of certified sustainable palm oil purchased</li>
</ul>
<p><a href="/wiki/GreenPalm" title="GreenPalm">GreenPalm</a> is one of the retailers executing the book and claim supply chain and trading programme. It guarantees that the palm oil producer is certified by the RSPO. Through GreenPalm the producer can certify a specified amount with the GreenPalm logo. The buyer of the oil is allowed to use the RSPO and the GreenPalm label for sustainable palm oil on his products.<sup id="cite_ref-GreenPalm_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GreenPalm-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Nutrition_and_health">Nutrition and health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_oil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Nutrition and health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Palm oil is an important source of calories and a food staple in poor communities.<sup id="cite_ref-WHO_Technical_Report_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WHO_Technical_Report-57">[57]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Economist_2011_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economist_2011-58">[58]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bradsher_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradsher-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>Much of the palm oil that is consumed as food is <a href="/wiki/Cooking_oil" title="Cooking oil">cooking oil</a>, to some degree oxidized rather than in the fresh state, and this oxidation appears to be responsible for the health risk associated with consuming palm oil.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Palmitic_acid">Palmitic acid</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_oil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Palmitic acid">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to studies reported on by the <a href="/wiki/Center_for_Science_in_the_Public_Interest" title="Center for Science in the Public Interest">Center for Science in the Public Interest</a> (CSPI), excessive intake of <a href="/wiki/Palmitic_acid" title="Palmitic acid">palmitic acid</a>, which makes up 44 percent of palm oil, increases blood cholesterol levels and may contribute to <a href="/wiki/Heart_disease" class="mw-redirect" title="Heart disease">heart disease</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CSPI_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CSPI-61">[61]</a></sup> The CSPI also reported that the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> and the US <a href="/wiki/National_Heart,_Lung_and_Blood_Institute" class="mw-redirect" title="National Heart, Lung and Blood Institute">National Heart, Lung and Blood Institute</a> have encouraged consumers to limit the consumption of palmitic acid and foods high in saturated fat.<sup id="cite_ref-WHO_Technical_Report_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WHO_Technical_Report-57">[57]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CSPI_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CSPI-61">[61]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a>, evidence is convincing that consumption of palmitic acid increases risk of developing cardiovascular diseases, placing it in the same evidence category as <a href="/wiki/Trans_fatty_acids" class="mw-redirect" title="Trans fatty acids">trans fatty acids</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Comparison_to_trans_fats">Comparison to trans fats</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_oil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Comparison to trans fats">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In response to negative reports on palm oil many food manufacturers transitioned to using hydrogenated vegetable oils in their products, which have also come under scrutiny for the impact these oils have on health.<sup id="cite_ref-McNamara_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McNamara-63">[63]</a></sup> A 2006 study supported by the <a href="/wiki/National_Institutes_of_Health" title="National Institutes of Health">National Institutes of Health</a> and the USDA <a href="/wiki/Agricultural_Research_Service" title="Agricultural Research Service">Agricultural Research Service</a> concluded that palm oil is not a safe substitute for partially hydrogenated fats (<a href="/wiki/Trans_fats" class="mw-redirect" title="Trans fats">trans fats</a>) in the food industry, because palm oil results in adverse changes in the blood concentrations of LDL cholesterol and <a href="/wiki/Apolipoprotein_B" title="Apolipoprotein B">apolipoprotein B</a> just as trans fat does.<sup id="cite_ref-ScienceDaily_LLC_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ScienceDaily_LLC-26">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Vega-L.C3.B3pez.2C_Sonia_et_al._54.E2.80.9362_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vega-L.C3.B3pez.2C_Sonia_et_al._54.E2.80.9362-64">[64]</a></sup> However, according to two reports published in 2010 by the Journal of the <a href="/wiki/American_College_of_Nutrition" title="American College of Nutrition">American College of Nutrition</a> palm oil is again an accepted replacement for hydrogenated vegetable oils<sup id="cite_ref-McNamara_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McNamara-63">[63]</a></sup> and a natural replacement for partially hydrogenated vegetable oils, which are a significant source of trans fats.<sup id="cite_ref-Hayes_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hayes-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Comparison_with_animal_saturated_fat">Comparison with animal saturated fat</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_oil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Comparison with animal saturated fat">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Not all saturated fats have equally cholesterolemic effects.<sup id="cite_ref-ng_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ng-66">[66]</a></sup> Studies have indicated that consumption of palm olein (which is more unsaturated) reduces blood cholesterol when compared to sources of saturated fats like <a href="/wiki/Coconut_oil" title="Coconut oil">coconut oil</a>, dairy and animal fats.<sup id="cite_ref-ng_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ng-66">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Acrolein">Acrolein</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_oil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Acrolein">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A 2009 study<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> tested the emission rates of <a href="/wiki/Acrolein" title="Acrolein">acrolein</a>, a toxic and malodorous breakdown product from <a href="/wiki/Glycerol" title="Glycerol">glycerol</a>, from the deep-frying of potatoes in red palm, olive, and polyunsaturated sunflower oils. The study found higher acrolein emission rates from the polyunsaturated sunflower oil (the scientists characterized red palm oil as "mono-unsaturated") and lower rates from both palm and olive oils. The <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> established a tolerable oral acrolein intake of 7.5&#160;mg/day per kilogram of body weight. Although acrolein occurs in <a href="/wiki/French_fries" title="French fries">French fries</a>, the levels are only a few micrograms per kilogram. A 2011 study concluded a health risk from acrolein in food is unlikely.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_and_environmental_impacts">Social and environmental impacts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_oil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Social and environmental impacts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Social_and_environmental_impact_of_palm_oil" title="Social and environmental impact of palm oil">Social and environmental impact of palm oil</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Social">Social</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_oil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Social">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Palm_forest.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Palm_forest.jpg/250px-Palm_forest.jpg" width="250" height="556" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Palm_forest.jpg/375px-Palm_forest.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Palm_forest.jpg/500px-Palm_forest.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1438" data-file-height="3196" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Palm_forest.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
In <a href="/wiki/Borneo" title="Borneo">Borneo</a>, the forest (F), is being replaced by oil palm plantations (G). These changes are irreversible for all practical purposes (H).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The palm oil industry has had both positive and negative impacts on workers, <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">indigenous peoples</a> and residents of palm oil-producing communities. Palm oil production provides employment opportunities, and has been shown to improve <a href="/wiki/Infrastructure" title="Infrastructure">infrastructure</a>, social services and reduce poverty.<sup id="cite_ref-Budidarsono_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Budidarsono-70">[70]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Norwana_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Norwana-71">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ismail_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ismail-72">[72]</a></sup> However, in some cases, oil palm plantations have developed lands without consultation or compensation of the indigenous people occupying the land, resulting in social conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-IDMC_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IDMC-73">[73]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Colchester_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colchester-74">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FPP_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FPP-75">[75]</a></sup> The use of <a href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration" title="Illegal immigration">illegal immigrants</a> in Malaysia has also raised concerns about working conditions within the palm oil industry.<sup id="cite_ref-BMS_2012_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BMS_2012-76">[76]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ABC_2014_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC_2014-77">[77]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC_2013_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_2013-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some social initiatives use palm oil cultivation as part of poverty alleviation strategies. Examples include the UN Food and Agriculture Organisation's hybrid oil palm project in Western <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a>, which improves incomes and diets of local populations,<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> and Malaysia's <a href="/wiki/Federal_Land_Development_Authority" title="Federal Land Development Authority">Federal Land Development Authority</a> and Federal Land Consolidation and Rehabilitation Authority, which both support rural development.<sup id="cite_ref-Ibrahim_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ibrahim-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Food_vs._fuel">Food vs. fuel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_oil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Food vs. fuel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Food_vs._fuel" title="Food vs. fuel">Food vs. fuel</a></div>
<p>The use of palm oil in the production of biodiesel has led to concerns that the need for fuel is being placed ahead of the need for food, leading to malnourishment in developing nations. This is known as the <a href="/wiki/Food_vs._fuel" title="Food vs. fuel">food versus fuel</a> debate. According to a 2008 report published in the <i><a href="/wiki/Renewable_and_Sustainable_Energy_Reviews" title="Renewable and Sustainable Energy Reviews">Renewable and Sustainable Energy Reviews</a></i>, palm oil was determined to be a sustainable source of both food and biofuel. The production of palm oil biodiesel does not pose a threat to edible palm oil supplies.<sup id="cite_ref-Man_Kee_Lam_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Man_Kee_Lam-81">[81]</a></sup> According to a 2009 study published in the <i>Environmental Science and Policy</i> journal, palm oil biodiesel might increase the demand for palm oil in the future, resulting in the expansion of palm oil production, and therefore an increased supply of food.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental">Environmental</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_oil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Environmental">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/2015_Southeast_Asian_haze" title="2015 Southeast Asian haze">2015 Southeast Asian haze</a></div>
<p>Palm oil cultivation has been criticized for impacts on the natural environment,<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Greenpeace_Cooking_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greenpeace_Cooking-84">[84]</a></sup> including <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">deforestation</a>, loss of natural habitats,<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> which has threatened <a href="/wiki/Critically_endangered_species" class="mw-redirect" title="Critically endangered species">critically endangered species</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/Orangutan" title="Orangutan">orangutan</a><sup id="cite_ref-cspi_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cspi-86">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Mail_Online_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mail_Online-87">[87]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Sumatran_tiger" title="Sumatran tiger">Sumatran tiger</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-WWF_2010_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WWF_2010-88">[88]</a></sup> and increased <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gas</a> emissions.<sup id="cite_ref-Greenpeace_Cooking_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greenpeace_Cooking-84">[84]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Foster_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Foster-89">[89]</a></sup> Many palm oil plantations are built on top of existing peat bogs, and clearing the land for palm oil cultivation contributes to rising greenhouse gas emissions.<sup id="cite_ref-Foster_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Foster-89">[89]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Rosenthal_NYT_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rosenthal_NYT-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>Efforts to portray palm oil cultivation as sustainable have been made by organizations including the <a href="/wiki/Roundtable_on_Sustainable_Palm_Oil" title="Roundtable on Sustainable Palm Oil">Roundtable on Sustainable Palm Oil</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Adnan_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Adnan-91">[91]</a></sup> an industry group, and the Malaysian government, which has committed to preserve 50 percent of its total land area as forest.<sup id="cite_ref-Morales_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Morales-10">[10]</a></sup> According to research conducted by the Tropical Peat Research Laboratory, a group studying palm oil cultivation in support of the industry,<sup id="cite_ref-Masilamany_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Masilamany-92">[92]</a></sup> oil palm plantations act as <a href="/wiki/Carbon_sink" title="Carbon sink">carbon sinks</a>, converting carbon dioxide into oxygen<sup id="cite_ref-New_Straits_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-New_Straits-93">[93]</a></sup> and, according to Malaysia's Second National Communication to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Framework_Convention_on_Climate_Change" title="United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change">United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change</a>, the plantations contribute to Malaysia's status as a net carbon sink.<sup id="cite_ref-NC2_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NC2-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>Environmental groups such as <a href="/wiki/Greenpeace" title="Greenpeace">Greenpeace</a> and <a href="/wiki/Friends_of_the_Earth" title="Friends of the Earth">Friends of the Earth</a> oppose the use of palm oil biofuels, claiming that the <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">deforestation</a> caused by oil palm plantations is more damaging for the climate than the benefits gained by switching to biofuel and utilizing the palms as carbon sinks.<sup id="cite_ref-Rosenthal_NYT_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rosenthal_NYT-90">[90]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pachter_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pachter-95">[95]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>While only 5 percent of the world's vegetable oil farmland is used for palm plantations, palm cultivation produces 38 percent of the world's total vegetable oil supply.<sup id="cite_ref-spinks_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spinks-97">[97]</a></sup> In terms of oil yield, a palm plantation is 10 times more productive than soya bean and rapeseed cultivation because the palm fruit and <a href="/wiki/Seed" title="Seed">kernel</a> both provide usable oil.<sup id="cite_ref-spinks_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spinks-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roundtable_On_Sustainable_Palm_Oil_.28RSPO.29">Roundtable On Sustainable Palm Oil (RSPO)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_oil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Roundtable On Sustainable Palm Oil (RSPO)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Roundtable_on_Sustainable_Palm_Oil" title="Roundtable on Sustainable Palm Oil">Roundtable on Sustainable Palm Oil</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Zurich_RT2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="RT2 (Roundtable No 2) in Zurich in 2005." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Zurich_RT2.jpg/250px-Zurich_RT2.jpg" width="250" height="185" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Zurich_RT2.jpg/375px-Zurich_RT2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Zurich_RT2.jpg/500px-Zurich_RT2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2537" data-file-height="1876" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Zurich_RT2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Roundtable No 2 (RT2) in Zurich in 2005.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <b>Roundtable on Sustainable Palm Oil</b> (RSPO) was created in 2004<sup id="cite_ref-Browne_53-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browne-53">[53]</a></sup> following concerns raised by non-governmental organizations about environmental impacts related to palm oil production. The organization has established international standards for sustainable palm oil production.<sup id="cite_ref-Gunasegaran_54-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gunasegaran-54">[54]</a></sup> Products containing <b>Certified Sustainable Palm Oil (CSPO)</b> can carry the RSPO trademark.<sup id="cite_ref-Yulisman_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yulisman-55">[55]</a></sup> Members of the RSPO include palm oil producers, environmental groups and manufacturers who use palm oil in their products.<sup id="cite_ref-Browne_53-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browne-53">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gunasegaran_54-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gunasegaran-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>Palm oil growers who produce Certified Sustainable Palm Oil have been critical of the organization because, though they have met RSPO standards and assumed the costs associated with certification, the market demand for certified palm oil remains low.<sup id="cite_ref-Gunasegaran_54-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gunasegaran-54">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Yulisman_55-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yulisman-55">[55]</a></sup> Low market demand has been attributed to the higher cost of Certified Sustainable Palm Oil, leading palm oil buyers to purchase cheaper non-certified palm oil. Palm oil is mostly <a href="/wiki/Fungible" class="mw-redirect" title="Fungible">fungible</a>. In 2011, 12% of palm oil produced was certified "sustainable", though only half of that had the RSPO label.<sup id="cite_ref-Watson_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Watson-98">[98]</a></sup> Even with such a low proportion being certified, <a href="/wiki/Greenpeace" title="Greenpeace">Greenpeace</a> has argued that confectioners are avoiding responsibilities on sustainable palm oil, because it says that RSPO standards fall short of protecting rain forests and reducing greenhouse gases.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
